top:100px; border-width:24.868988716486px 96.858316112863px 0 0; border-top-color:Red"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Red"></div>\n<div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:0; border-width:0 72.654252800536px 100px 0; border-right-color:DodgerBlue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;right:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<p>Religion in South Carolina<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PewReligionSC_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-PewReligionSC-70">[66]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0Evangelical Protestant (35%)</div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Red; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0Unaffiliated (19%)</div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Purple; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0Mainline Protestant (16%)</div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:LightBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0Black Protestant (15%)</div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0Catholic (10%)</div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Orange; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0Other Christian (3%)</div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkGreen; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0Other (3%)</div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0Don\'t Know (1%)</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Religion_Data_Archives" title="Association of Religion Data Archives">Association of Religion Data Archives</a> (ARDA), in 2010 the largest denominations were the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a> with 913,763 adherents, the <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">United Methodist Church</a> with 274,111 adherents, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> with 181,743 adherents. Fourth largest is the <a href="/wiki/African_Methodist_Episcopal_Church" title="African Methodist Episcopal Church">African Methodist Episcopal Church</a> with 564 congregations and 121,000 members and fifth largest is the <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_(USA)" title="Presbyterian Church (USA)">Presbyterian Church (USA)</a> with 320 congregations and almost 100,000 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-71">[67]</a></sup></p>\n<p>As of 2010, South Carolina is the American state with the highest per capita proportion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baha%27is" title="Baha\'is">Baha\'is</a> with 17,559 adherents,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[68]</a></sup> making the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baha%27i_Faith" title="Baha\'i Faith">Baha\'i Faith</a> the second largest religion in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[69]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_cities">Major cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Major cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2016, the US Census Bureau released 2015 population estimates for South Carolina\'s most populous cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[70]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Carolina_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="South Carolina locations by per capita income">South Carolina locations by per capita income</a></div>\n<div class="center">\n<div class="thumb tnone">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arthur_Ravenel_Bridge_(from_water).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1116" data-file-width="3888" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Arthur_Ravenel_Bridge_%28from_water%29.jpg/750px-Arthur_Ravenel_Bridge_%28from_water%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Arthur_Ravenel_Bridge_%28from_water%29.jpg/1125px-Arthur_Ravenel_Bridge_%28from_water%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Arthur_Ravenel_Bridge_%28from_water%29.jpg/1500px-Arthur_Ravenel_Bridge_%28from_water%29.jpg 2x" width="750"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arthur_Ravenel_Bridge_(from_water).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<center>The <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Ravenel_Jr._Bridge" title="Arthur Ravenel Jr. Bridge">Arthur Ravenel Jr. Bridge</a> from Charleston Harbor</center>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>According to the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Economic_Analysis" title="Bureau of Economic Analysis">Bureau of Economic Analysis</a>, South Carolina\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_state_product" title="Gross state product">gross state product</a> (GSP) in current dollars was $97 billion in 1997 and $153 billion in 2007. Its per-capita real gross domestic product (GDP) in <a href="/wiki/Chained_dollars" title="Chained dollars">chained 2000 dollars</a> was $26,772 in 1997 and $28,894 in 2007; that represents 85% of the $31,619 per-capita real GDP for the United States overall in 1997, and 76% of the $38,020 for the U.S. in 2007. The state debt in 2012 was calculated by one source to be $22.9bn, or $7,800 per taxpayer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[72]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Major agricultural outputs of the state are tobacco, poultry, cotton, cattle, dairy products, soybeans, hay, rice, and swine. Industrial outputs include textile goods, chemical products, paper products, machinery, automobiles, automotive products and tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[74]</a></sup> According to the Bureau of Labor Statistics, as of March 2012, South Carolina had 1,852,700 nonfarm jobs of which 12% are in manufacturing, 11.5% are in leisure and hospitality, 19% are in trade, transportation, and utilities, and 11.8% are in education and health services. The service sector accounts for 83.7% of the South Carolina economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[75]</a></sup></p>\n<p>During the economic downturn in the Late 2000s Recession, South Carolina\'s Unemployment Rate peaked at 12.0% in November and December 2009. It is continuing a steady decline with an unemployment rate of 8.9% as of March 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[76]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Margate_Tower_6-7-17.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="530" data-file-width="480" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Margate_Tower_6-7-17.png/220px-Margate_Tower_6-7-17.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Margate_Tower_6-7-17.png/330px-Margate_Tower_6-7-17.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Margate_Tower_6-7-17.png/440px-Margate_Tower_6-7-17.png 2x" width="220"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Margate_Tower_6-7-17.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMargate Hotel Tower in Myrtle Beach</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Many large corporations have moved their locations to South Carolina. <a href="/wiki/Boeing_South_Carolina" title="Boeing South Carolina">Boeing</a> opened an aircraft manufacturing facility in Charleston in 2011, which serves as one of two final assembly sites for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/787_Dreamliner" title="787 Dreamliner">787 Dreamliner</a>. South Carolina is a right-to-work state<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[77]</a></sup> and many businesses utilize staffing agencies to temporarily fill positions. Domtar, located in Rock Hill, is the only Fortune 500 company headquartered in South Carolina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[78]</a></sup> The Fortune 1000 list includes <a href="/wiki/SCANA" title="SCANA">SCANA</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sonoco_Products" title="Sonoco Products">Sonoco Products</a> and ScanSource.</p>\n<p>South Carolina also benefits from foreign investment. There are 1,950 foreign-owned firms operating in South Carolina employing almost 135,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[79]</a></sup> Foreign Direct Investment (FDI) brought 1.06 billion dollars to the state economy in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[80]</a></sup> Since 1994, <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a> has had a production facility in Spartanburg County near Greer.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>\n<td class="mbox-text">\n<div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(March 2017)</i></small></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:South_Carolina_media" title="Category:South Carolina media">Category:South Carolina media</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_arts">The arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: The arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_literature" title="South Carolina literature">South Carolina literature</a></div>\n<p>South Carolina has many venues for visual and performing arts. The <a href="/wiki/Gibbes_Museum_of_Art" title="Gibbes Museum of Art">Gibbes Museum of Art</a> in Charleston, the <a href="/wiki/Greenville_County_Museum_of_Art" title="Greenville County Museum of Art">Greenville County Museum of Art</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Museum_of_Art" title="Columbia Museum of Art">Columbia Museum of Art</a>, Spartanburg Art Museum, and the <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_State_Museum" title="South Carolina State Museum">South Carolina State Museum</a> in Columbia among others provide access to visual arts to the state. There are also numerous historic sites and museums scattered throughout the state paying homage to many events and periods in the state\'s history from Native American inhabitation to the present day.</p>\n<p>South Carolina also has performing art venues including the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Center" title="Peace Center">Peace Center</a> in Greenville, the <a href="/wiki/Koger_Center_for_the_Arts" title="Koger Center for the Arts">Koger Center for the Arts</a> in Columbia, and the <a href="/wiki/Newberry_Opera_House" title="Newberry Opera House">Newberry Opera House</a>, among others to bring local, national, and international talent to the stages of South Carolina. There are several large venues in the state that can house major events, such as <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Life_Arena" title="Colonial Life Arena">Colonial Life Arena</a> in Columbia, <a href="/wiki/Bon_Secours_Wellness_Arena" title="Bon Secours Wellness Arena">Bon Secours Wellness Arena</a> in Greenville, and <a href="/wiki/North_Charleston_Coliseum" title="North Charleston Coliseum">North Charleston Coliseum</a>.</p>\n<p>One of the nation\'s major performing arts festivals, <a href="/wiki/Spoleto_Festival_USA" title="Spoleto Festival USA">Spoleto Festival USA</a>, is held annually in Charleston. There are also countless local festivals throughout the state highlighting many cultural traditions, historical events, and folklore.</p>\n<p>According to the South Carolina Arts Commission, creative industries generate $9.2 billion annually and support over 78,000 jobs in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[81]</a></sup> A 2009 statewide poll by the University of South Carolina Institute for Public Service and Policy Research found that 67% of residents had participated in the arts in some form during the past year and on average citizens had participated in the arts 14 times in the previous year.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:I-26_(SC).svg"><img alt="I-26 (SC).svg" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="601" height="70" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/I-26_%28SC%29.svg/70px-I-26_%28SC%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/I-26_%28SC%29.svg/105px-I-26_%28SC%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/I-26_%28SC%29.svg/140px-I-26_%28SC%29.svg.png 2x" width="70"/></a></div>\n<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_76.svg"><img alt="US 76.svg" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="70" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/US_76.svg/70px-US_76.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/US_76.svg/105px-US_76.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/US_76.svg/140px-US_76.svg.png 2x" width="70"/></a></div>\n<div class="floatright"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:South_Carolina_9.svg"><img alt="South Carolina 9.svg" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="750" height="70" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/South_Carolina_9.svg/88px-South_Carolina_9.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/South_Carolina_9.svg/132px-South_Carolina_9.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/South_Carolina_9.svg/176px-South_Carolina_9.svg.png 2x" width="88"/></a></div>\n<p>The state has the fourth largest state-maintained system in the country, consisting of 11 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Interstate_Highways_in_South_Carolina" title="List of Interstate Highways in South Carolina">Interstates</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_numbered_highways_in_South_Carolina" title="List of numbered highways in South Carolina">numbered highways</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_highways" title="State highways">state highways</a>, and secondary roads, totalling approximately 41,500 miles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STIP_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-STIP-86">[82]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On secondary roads, South Carolina uses a numbering system to keep track of all non-interstate and primary highways that are maintained by the <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Department_of_Transportation" title="South Carolina Department of Transportation">South Carolina Department of Transportation</a>. Secondary roads are numbered by the number of the county followed by a unique number for the particular road.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Passenger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> operates four passenger routes in South Carolina: the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crescent_(Amtrak)" title="Crescent (Amtrak)">Crescent</a></i>, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palmetto_(Amtrak)" title="Palmetto (Amtrak)">Palmetto</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Silver_Meteor" title="Silver Meteor">Silver Meteor</a></i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Silver_Star_(Amtrak_train)" title="Silver Star (Amtrak train)">Silver Star</a></i>. The <i>Crescent</i> route serves the Upstate cities, the <i>Silver Star</i> serves the Midlands cities, and the <i>Palmetto</i> and <i>Silver Meteor</i> routes serve the low country cities.</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Station_stops">Station stops</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Station stops">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tr>\n<th>Station</th>\n<th>Connections</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Camden_(Amtrak_station)" title="Camden (Amtrak station)">Camden</a></td>\n<td>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005480; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0<i><a href="/wiki/Silver_Star_(Amtrak_train)" title="Silver Star (Amtrak train)">Silver Star</a></i></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina_(Amtrak_station)" title="Charleston, South Carolina (Amtrak station)">North Charleston</a></td>\n<td>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005480; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0<i><a href="/wiki/Palmetto_(train)" title="Palmetto (train)">Palmetto</a></i></div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005480; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0<i><a href="/wiki/Silver_Meteor" title="Silver Meteor">Silver Meteor</a></i></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Columbia_station_(South_Carolina)" title="Columbia station (South Carolina)">Columbia</a></td>\n<td>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005480; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0<i><a href="/wiki/Silver_Star_(Amtrak_train)" title="Silver Star (Amtrak train)">Silver Star</a></i></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clemson_(Amtrak_station)" title="Clemson (Amtrak station)">Clemson</a></td>\n<td>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005480; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0<i><a href="/wiki/Crescent_(train)" title="Crescent (train)">Crescent</a></i></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denmark_(Amtrak_station)" title="Denmark (Amtrak station)">Denmark</a></td>\n<td>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005480; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0<i><a href="/wiki/Silver_Star_(Amtrak_train)" title="Silver Star (Amtrak train)">Silver Star</a></i></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dillon_(Amtrak_station)" title="Dillon (Amtrak station)">Dillon</a></td>\n<td>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005480; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0<i><a href="/wiki/Palmetto_(train)" title="Palmetto (train)">Palmetto</a></i></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florence_(Amtrak_station)" title="Florence (Amtrak station)">Florence</a></td>\n<td>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005480; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0<i><a href="/wiki/Palmetto_(train)" title="Palmetto (train)">Palmetto</a></i></div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005480; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0<i><a href="/wiki/Silver_Meteor" title="Silver Meteor">Silver Meteor</a></i></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenville_(Amtrak_station)" title="Greenville (Amtrak station)">Greenville</a></td>\n<td>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005480; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0<i><a href="/wiki/Crescent_(train)" title="Crescent (train)">Crescent</a></i></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingstree_(Amtrak_station)" title="Kingstree (Amtrak station)">Kingstree</a></td>\n<td>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005480; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0<i><a href="/wiki/Silver_Meteor" title="Silver Meteor">Silver Meteor</a></i></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spartanburg_(Amtrak_station)" title="Spartanburg (Amtrak station)">Spartanburg</a></td>\n<td>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005480; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0<i><a href="/wiki/Crescent_(train)" title="Crescent (train)">Crescent</a></i></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yemassee_(Amtrak_station)" title="Yemassee (Amtrak station)">Yemassee</a></td>\n<td>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005480; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0<i><a href="/wiki/Palmetto_(train)" title="Palmetto (train)">Palmetto</a></i></div>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #005480; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\xc2\xa0</span>\xc2\xa0<i><a href="/wiki/Silver_Meteor" title="Silver Meteor">Silver Meteor</a></i></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Freight">Freight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Freight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation" title="CSX Transportation">CSX Transportation</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern" title="Norfolk Southern">Norfolk Southern</a> are the only Class I railroad companies in South Carolina, as other freight companies in the state are short lines.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_and_regional_airports">Major and regional airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Major and regional airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_South_Carolina" title="List of airports in South Carolina">List of airports in South Carolina</a></div>\n<p>There are seven significant airports in South Carolina, all of which act as regional airport hubs. The busiest by passenger volume is Charleston International Airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[83]</a></sup> Just across the border in North Carolina is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charlotte/Douglas_International_Airport" title="Charlotte/Douglas International Airport">Charlotte/Douglas International Airport</a>, the 30th busiest airport in the world, in terms of passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[84]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Columbia_Metropolitan_Airport" title="Columbia Metropolitan Airport">Columbia Metropolitan Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Columbia</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Charleston_International_Airport" title="Charleston International Airport">Charleston International Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 North Charleston</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenville-Spartanburg_International_Airport" title="Greenville-Spartanburg International Airport">Greenville-Spartanburg International Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Greenville/Spartanburg</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Florence_Regional_Airport" title="Florence Regional Airport">Florence Regional Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Florence</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Myrtle_Beach_International_Airport" title="Myrtle Beach International Airport">Myrtle Beach International Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Myrtle Beach</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hilton_Head_Airport" title="Hilton Head Airport">Hilton Head Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Hilton Head Island/Beaufort</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rock_Hill/York_County_Airport" title="Rock Hill/York County Airport">Rock Hill/York County Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Rock Hill</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_government_and_politics" title="South Carolina government and politics">South Carolina government and politics</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SCCapitol0270.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/SCCapitol0270.jpg/300px-SCCapitol0270.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/SCCapitol0270.jpg/450px-SCCapitol0270.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/SCCapitol0270.jpg/600px-SCCapitol0270.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SCCapitol0270.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_State_House" title="South Carolina State House">South Carolina State House</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>South Carolina\'s <a href="/wiki/State_governments_of_the_United_States" title="State governments of the United States">state government</a> consists of the Executive, Legislative, and Judicial branches. Also relevant are the state constitution, law enforcement agencies, federal representation, state finances, and state taxes.</p>\n<p>South Carolina has historically had a weak executive branch and a strong legislature. Before 1865, governors in South Carolina were appointed by the General Assembly, and held the title "President of State." The 1865 Constitution changed this process, requiring a popular election. Local governments were also weak. But, the 1867 Constitution, passed during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reconstruction_era_(United_States)" title="Reconstruction era (United States)">Reconstruction era</a>, extended democratization by establishing <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">home rule</a> for counties, which were established from the former designated districts of the state.</p>\n<p>The 1895 state constitution overturned this, reducing the role of counties and strengthening the relative role of the state legislature; essentially the counties were agents of the state and ruled by the General Assembly through the legislative delegation for each county.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-governance_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-governance-28">[28]</a></sup> They are geographically comprehensive; all areas of the state are included in counties. As each county had one state senator, that position was particularly powerful. This status continued until 1973, when the state constitution was amended to provide for <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">home rule</a> for the counties. During this time the state had changed, with increasing urbanization, but rural counties retained proportionally more power as the legislature was based in representatives elected from counties rather than population districts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tyler_1998_p._222_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tyler_1998_p._222-89">[85]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The federal court case, <i><a href="/wiki/Reynolds_v._Sims" title="Reynolds v. Sims">Reynolds v. Sims</a></i> (1964), "established the one-man, one-vote concept for electoral representation at the state level. Legislators were now supposed to represent more or less equal numbers of people."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tyler_1998_p._222_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tyler_1998_p._222-89">[85]</a></sup> Residents of urban areas had been found to be markedly underrepresented in the legislature under the county-based system. Reapportionment made obvious the need for other changes to county structure, leading to the legislature passing the constitutional amendment. The Home Rule Act of 1975 implemented the amendment giving more power to the counties. With urbanization their governments have become increasingly important in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tyler_1998_p._222_89-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tyler_1998_p._222-89">[85]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Several changes to the state constitution have affected the office of the governor and the cabinet. In 1926 the governor\'s term was extended from two to four years; in 1982 the governor was allowed to run for a second succeeding term. In 1993, the state passed an amendment requiring a limited cabinet (all of whom must be popularly elected).</p>\n<p>As of January 2, 2016, there were 2,948,772 registered voters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[87]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>As of 2010, South Carolina is one of three states that has not agreed to use competitive international <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Math" title="Math">math</a> and <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">language</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Educational_standards" title="Educational standards">standards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[88]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 2014, the <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Supreme_Court" title="South Carolina Supreme Court">South Carolina Supreme Court</a> ruled that the state had failed to provide a "minimally adequate" education to children in all parts of the state as required by the state\'s constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[89]</a></sup></p>\n<p>South Carolina has 1,144 K\xe2\x80\x9312 schools in 85 school districts with an enrollment of 712,244 as of fall 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[91]</a></sup> As of the 2008\xe2\x80\x932009 school year, South Carolina spent $9,450 per student which places it 31st in the country for per student spending.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[92]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 2015, the national average SAT score was 1490 and the South Carolina average was 1442, only around 50 points lower than the national average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[93]</a></sup></p>\n<p>South Carolina is the only state which owns and operates its own statewide school bus system. As of December 2016, the state maintains a 5,582 bus fleet with the average vehicle in service being 15 years old with 236,000 miles, compared to the national average of 6 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[94]</a></sup> Half of the state\'s school buses are more than 15 years old and some are reportedly up to 30 years old. In 2017 in the budget proposal, Superintendent of Education Molly Spearman requested that the state lease to purchase 1,000 buses to replace the most decrepit vehicles. An additional 175 buses could be purchased immediately through the State Treasurer\'s master lease program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[95]</a></sup> On January 5, 2017, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="U.S. Environmental Protection Agency">U.S. Environmental Protection Agency</a> awarded South Carolina more than $1.1 million to replace 57 school buses with new cleaner models through its <a href="/wiki/Diesel_Emissions_Reduction_Act" title="Diesel Emissions Reduction Act">Diesel Emissions Reduction Act</a> program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[96]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Institutions_of_higher_education">Institutions of higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Institutions of higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_South_Carolina" title="List of colleges and universities in South Carolina">List of colleges and universities in South Carolina</a></div>\n<p>South Carolina has a diverse group of institutions of higher education, from large state-funded research universities to small colleges that cultivate a liberal arts, religious or military tradition, including the following:</p>\n<dl>\n<dd><i>Listed in order of date of founding</i></dd>\n</dl>\n<ul>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/College_of_Charleston" title="College of Charleston">College of Charleston</a>, founded in 1770 and chartered in 1785, is the oldest institution of higher learning in South Carolina, the 13th oldest in the United States, and the first <a href="/wiki/Municipal_college" title="Municipal college">municipal college</a> in the country. The college is in company with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonial_Colleges" title="Colonial Colleges">Colonial Colleges</a> as one of the original and foundational institutions of higher education in the United States. Its founders include three signers of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">United States Declaration of Independence</a> and three signers of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a>. The college\'s historic campus, which is listed on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_the_Interior" title="U.S. Department of the Interior">U.S. Department of the Interior</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>, forms an integral part of Charleston\'s colonial-era urban center. The Graduate School of the College of Charleston offers a number of degree programs and coordinates support for its nationally recognized faculty research efforts.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_South_Carolina" title="University of South Carolina">University of South Carolina</a>, located in Columbia, is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flagship_campus" title="Flagship campus">flagship</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_university_(U.S.)" title="State university (U.S.)">public</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Co-education" title="Co-education">co-educational</a>, <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">research university</a> with seven satellite campuses. The institution was founded in 1801 as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Carolina_College" title="South Carolina College">South Carolina College</a>, and its original campus, <a href="/wiki/Old_Campus_District,_University_of_South_Carolina" title="Old Campus District, University of South Carolina">The Horseshoe</a>, is listed on the National Register of Historic Places. The university\'s main campus covers over 359 acres (1.5\xc2\xa0km<sup>2</sup>) in the urban core less than one city block from the <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_State_House" title="South Carolina State House">South Carolina State House</a>. The University of South Carolina maintains an enrollment of over 32,800 students on the Columbia campus.</li>\n</ul>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Furman-Belltower2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="333" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Furman-Belltower2.jpg/250px-Furman-Belltower2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Furman-Belltower2.jpg/375px-Furman-Belltower2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Furman-Belltower2.jpg/500px-Furman-Belltower2.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Furman-Belltower2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Furman_University" title="Furman University">Furman University</a> bell tower near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenville,_SC" title="Greenville, SC">Greenville</a>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Furman_University" title="Furman University">Furman University</a> is a private, coeducational, non-sectarian, liberal arts university in <a href="/wiki/Greenville,_South_Carolina" title="Greenville, South Carolina">Greenville</a>. Founded in 1826, Furman enrolls approximately 2,600 undergraduate and 500 graduate students. Furman is the largest private institution in South Carolina. The university is primarily focused on undergraduate education (only two departments, education and chemistry, offer graduate degrees).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Erskine_College" title="Erskine College">Erskine College</a> is a private, coeducational liberal arts college located in <a href="/wiki/Due_West,_South_Carolina" title="Due West, South Carolina">Due West, South Carolina</a>. The college was founded in 1839 and is affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Associate_Reformed_Presbyterian_Church" title="Associate Reformed Presbyterian Church">Associate Reformed Presbyterian Church</a>, which maintains a theological seminary on the campus.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/The_Citadel,_The_Military_College_of_South_Carolina" title="The Citadel, The Military College of South Carolina">The Citadel, The Military College of South Carolina</a> is a state-supported, comprehensive college located in Charleston. Founded in 1842, the college is best known for its undergraduate Corps of Cadets military program for men and women, which combines academics, physical challenges and military discipline. In addition to the cadet program, civilian programs are offered through The Citadel Graduate College with its evening certificate, undergraduate and graduate programs. The Citadel enrolls 2,200 undergraduate cadets in its residential military program and 1,200 civilian students in the evening programs.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Wofford_College" title="Wofford College">Wofford College</a> is a small liberal arts college located in <a href="/wiki/Spartanburg,_South_Carolina" title="Spartanburg, South Carolina">Spartanburg</a>. Wofford was founded in 1854 with a bequest of $100,000 from the Rev. Benjamin Wofford (1780\xe2\x80\x931850), a Methodist minister and Spartanburg native who sought to create a college for "literary, classical, and scientific education in my native district of Spartanburg." Wofford is one of the few four-year institutions in the southeastern United States founded before the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> and still operating on its original campus.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Newberry_College" title="Newberry College">Newberry College</a> is a small liberal arts college located in <a href="/wiki/Newberry,_South_Carolina" title="Newberry, South Carolina">Newberry</a>.Newberry was founded in 1856 and is a co-educational, private liberal-arts college of the Evangelical Lutheran Church in America (ELCA) located on a historic 90-acre (36 ha) campus in Newberry, South Carolina. The college has 1,042 students and a 14:1 student-teacher ratio. According to U.S. News &amp; World Report\'s America\'s Best Colleges, Newberry College ranks among the nation\'s top colleges in the southern region.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Claflin_University" title="Claflin University">Claflin University</a>, founded in 1869 by the <a href="/wiki/American_Missionary_Association" title="American Missionary Association">American Missionary Association</a>, is the oldest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historically_black_college" title="Historically black college">historically black college</a> in the state. After the Democratic-dominated legislature closed the university in 1877, before passing a law to restrict admission to whites, it designated Claflin as the only state college for blacks.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lander_University" title="Lander University">Lander University</a> is a public liberal arts university located in <a href="/wiki/Greenwood,_South_Carolina" title="Greenwood, South Carolina">Greenwood</a>. Lander was founded in 1872 as Willamston Female College.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[97]</a></sup> The school relocated to Greenwood in 1904 and was renamed Lander College in honor of its founder, Samuel Lander. In 1973 Lander became part of the state\'s higher education system and is now a co-educational institution. The university is focused on undergraduate education and currently enrolls approximately 2,800 undergraduates.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_College" title="Presbyterian College">Presbyterian College</a> (PC) is a private liberal arts college founded in 1880 in Clinton. Presbyterian College is affiliated with the Presbyterian Church USA, and enrolls around 1300 undergraduate students. In 2007, <i>Washington Monthly</i> ranked PC as the No. 1 Liberal Arts College in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[98]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Winthrop_University" title="Winthrop University">Winthrop University</a>, founded in 1886 as an all-female teaching school in <a href="/wiki/Rock_Hill,_South_Carolina" title="Rock Hill, South Carolina">Rock Hill</a>, became a co-ed institution in 1974. Winthrop is now a public university that has an enrollment of just over 6,000 students. It is one of the fastest growing universities in the state, with several new academic and recreational buildings being added to the main campus in the past five years, as well as several more planned for the near future. The Richard W. Riley College of Education is still the school\'s most well-known area of study.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Clemson_University" title="Clemson University">Clemson University</a>, founded in 1889, is a public, coeducational, <a href="/wiki/Land-grant_university" title="Land-grant university">land-grant</a> research university located in <a href="/wiki/Clemson,_South_Carolina" title="Clemson, South Carolina">Clemson</a>. The school currently enrolls more than 18,000 students from all 50 states and from more than 70 countries. Clemson is also the home to the <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Botanical_Garden" title="South Carolina Botanical Garden">South Carolina Botanical Garden</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/North_Greenville_University" title="North Greenville University">North Greenville University</a>, founded in 1891, is a comprehensive university located in <a href="/wiki/Tigerville,_South_Carolina" title="Tigerville, South Carolina">Tigerville</a>. It is affiliated with South Carolina Baptist Convention and the Southern Baptist Convention, and is accredited by the Commission on Colleges of the Southern Association of Colleges and Schools. It has a current enrollment of around 2260 undergraduates.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_State_University" title="South Carolina State University">South Carolina State University</a>, founded in 1896, is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historically_black_university" title="Historically black university">historically black university</a> located in Orangeburg. SCSU has a current enrollment of nearly 5,000, and offers undergraduate, graduate and post-graduate degrees. SCSU boasts the only Doctor of Education program in the state.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Anderson_University_(South_Carolina)" title="Anderson University (South Carolina)">Anderson University</a>, founded in 1911, is a selective comprehensive university located in <a href="/wiki/Anderson,_South_Carolina" title="Anderson, South Carolina">Anderson</a>, offering bachelor\'s and master\'s degrees in approximately 50 areas of study. Anderson University currently enrolls around 2,300 students.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Webster_University" title="Webster University">Webster University</a>, founded in 1915 in St. Louis, MO, with 5 extended campuses in SC, offers undergraduate and graduate degrees.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bob_Jones_University" title="Bob Jones University">Bob Jones University</a>, founded in 1927, is a non-denominational University founded on fundamentalist Christian beliefs (e.g., inspiration and inerrancy of the Scriptures, the creation of man by the direct act of God, the fall of man, the "young earth" and flood geology, and man\'s need for personal faith in the finished work of the Lord Jesus Christ). BJU also offers over 60 undergraduate majors and has over 70 graduate programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[99]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Coastal_Carolina_University" title="Coastal Carolina University">Coastal Carolina University</a>, founded in 1954, became an independent state-supported liberal arts university in 1993. The university enrolls approximately 10,000 students on its 307-acre (1.24 km2) campus in Conway, part of the Myrtle Beach metropolitan area. Baccalaureate programs are offered in 51 major fields of study, along with graduate programs in education, business administration (MBA), and coastal marine and wetland studies.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Charleston_Southern_University" title="Charleston Southern University">Charleston Southern University</a>, founded in 1969, is a liberal arts university, and is affiliated with the South Carolina Baptist Convention. Charleston Southern (CSU) is located on 300 acres, formerly the site of a rice and indigo plantation, in the <a href="/wiki/North_Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="North Charleston, South Carolina">City of North Charleston</a> one of South Carolina\'s largest accredited, independent universities, enrolling approximately 3,200 students.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Francis_Marion_University" title="Francis Marion University">Francis Marion University</a>,(formerly Francis Marion College), is a state-supported liberal arts university located near <a href="/wiki/Florence,_South_Carolina" title="Florence, South Carolina">Florence, South Carolina</a>. It was founded in 1970. It achieved its university status in 1992.</li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span id="Universities_and_colleges_ranked_by_endowment,_2010"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[100]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">Health care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Health care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>For overall health care, South Carolina is ranked 33rd out of the 50 states, according to the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Fund" title="Commonwealth Fund">Commonwealth Fund</a>, a private health foundation working to improve the health care system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[101]</a></sup> The state\'s teen birth rate was 53 births per 1,000 teens, compared to the average of 41.9 births for the US, according to the <a href="/wiki/Kaiser_Family_Foundation" title="Kaiser Family Foundation">Kaiser Family Foundation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[102]</a></sup> The state\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" title="Infant mortality rate">infant mortality rate</a> was 9.4 deaths per 1,000 births compared to the US average of 6.9 deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[103]</a></sup></p>\n<p>There were 2.6 physicians per 1,000 people compared to the US average of 3.2 physicians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[104]</a></sup> There was $5,114 spent on health expenses per capita in the state, compared to the US average of $5,283.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[105]</a></sup> There were 26 percent of children and 13 percent of elderly living in poverty in the state, compared to 23 percent and 13 percent, respectively, doing so in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[106]</a></sup> And, 34 percent of children were <a href="/wiki/Overweight" title="Overweight">overweight</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obese" title="Obese">obese</a>, compared to the US average of 32 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[107]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_South_Carolina" title="Sports in South Carolina">Sports in South Carolina</a></div>\n<p>Although no major league professional sports teams are based in South Carolina, the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Panthers" title="Carolina Panthers">Carolina Panthers</a> do have training facilities in the state and played their Inaugural Season\'s home games at Clemson\'s Memorial Stadium. The Panthers consider themselves "The Carolinas\' Team" and refrained from naming themselves after Charlotte or either of the Carolinas. The state is also home to numerous minor league professional teams. College teams represent their particular South Carolina institutions, and are the primary options for football, basketball and baseball attendance in the state. South Carolina is also a top destination for golf and water sports.</p>\n<p>South Carolina is also home to one of NASCAR\'s first tracks and its first paved speedway, <a href="/wiki/Darlington_Raceway" title="Darlington Raceway">Darlington Raceway</a> northwest of Florence.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_lands_in_South_Carolina">Federal lands in South Carolina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Carolina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Federal lands in South Carolina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Congaree_swamp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="190" data-file-width="260" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Congaree_swamp.jpg/250px-Congaree_swamp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/81/Congaree_swamp.jpg 1.5x" width="250"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Congaree_swamp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Congaree_National_Park" title="Congaree National Park">Congaree National Park</a>, Hopkins</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_federal_lands_in_South_Carolina" title="List of federal lands in South Carolina">List of federal lands in South Carolina</a></div>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Pinckney_National_Historic_Site" title="Charles Pinckney National Historic Site">Charles Pinckney National Historic Site</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mt._Pleasant,_South_Carolina" title="Mt. Pleasant, South Carolina">Mt. Pleasant</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Congaree_National_Park" title="Congaree National Park">Congaree National Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hopkins,_South_Carolina" title="Hopkins, South Carolina">Hopkins</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cowpens_National_Battlefield" title="Cowpens National Battlefield">Cowpens National Battlefield</a> near <a href="/wiki/Chesnee,_South_Carolina" title="Chesnee, South Carolina">Chesnee</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Moultrie_National_Monument" title="Fort Moultrie National Monument">Fort Moultrie National Monument</a> at <a href="/wiki/Sullivan%27s_Island,_South_Carolina" title="Sullivan\'s Island, South Carolina">Sullivan\'s Island</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fort_Sumter_National_Monument" title="Fort Sumter National Monument">Fort Sumter National Monument</a> in <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston Harbor</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kings_Mountain_National_Military_Park" title="Kings Mountain National Military Park">Kings Mountain National Military Park</a> at <a href="/wiki/Blacksburg,_South_Carolina" title="Blacksburg, South Carolina">Blacksburg</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ninety_Six_National_Historic_Site" title="Ninety Six National Historic Site">Ninety Six National Historic Site</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ninety_Six,_South_Carolina" title="Ninety Six, South Carolina">Ninety Six</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Overmountain_Victory_National_Historic_Trail" title="Overmountain Victory National Historic Trail">Overmountain Victory National Historic Trail</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fort_Jackson_(South_Carolina)" title="Fort Jackson (South Carolina)">Fort Jackson</a> near <a href="/wiki/Columbia,_South_Carolina" title="Columbia, South Carolina">Columbia</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Joint_Base_Charleston" title="Joint Base Charleston">Joint Base Charleston</a> near <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Shaw_Air_Force_Base" title="Shaw Air Force Base">Shaw Air Force Base</a> near <a href="/wiki/Sumter,_South_Carolina" title="Sumter, South Carolina">Sumter</a></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallery">Gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
